1:20 I felt bad for the old lady to the left... I mean she's probably been around since the 1950s at least or possibly even 1940s, and now this is the world she finds herself in where crazy Japanese people go around in spandex suits acting insane. If I have to toil through another 50 years or so on this Earth, then when I'm approaching my last decade or two, I don't think Pink Guy is what I'm gonna want to see. Though the 2060s version of Pink Guy is probably gonna be... like... someone wearing a sort of electric suit that shows extremely bright colours in a stripe pattern going every which way, and they'll have like these sort of roller shoes but they can roll the person in ANY given direction, while on their hands are some sort of strange propulsion device not unlike Iron Man's, but not meant for flying in the air. 

So the hands are directed around them to propel them causing a sort of anime effect where putting their hands behind them make them run REAL fast even though the illusion is that they're moving SO fast that their arms drag behind them from wind resistance. They'll move strangely, but while doing flips, and the roller shoes/propulsion hands assist in those movement, while the strange sounds they make like Pink Guy will be altered by a tiny device in their mouths or worn on their throats that alter their voice immensely. The kids born in the 2040s-50s will get it, understand it, and maybe even have some basic idea of how all this shit works... but me? I grew up in a time when roller skates/shoes only go ONE way, propulsion hands were a work of fiction, there were some clothes with basic LED lights but nothing of any real complication that was available at an affordable price to the average consumer that could create the type of lighting effects I imagine being available on clothing 50 years from now, not to mention we still use physical currency like coins and bills. At least I still do anyways. Many people probably switched to credit cards entirely, but I think one day we won't even need those.

Smartphones will be so small that they can be worn as glasses and probably accessed by pointing at things in front of you that other people can't see. More complicated things like computers will be on wristwatches or, for those who require more than just a simple laptop-like device, something the size of a modern day smartphone would be able to do all the things a desktop computer could do and more. As for what desktop computers will be? Everything necessary will be in something the size of a modern flatscreen TV, and yes, it will have a screen on it, but you could of course purchase a larger one. Well, 'larger', the screen itself will be large, but it will be a sort of holographic screen. It won't really be there. Videogames will no longer need keyboards or controllers; a sort of hat or helmet will allow you to control the game with your thoughts. Voice command will be at such a level of efficiency that no matter what accent you may have, or even if you're terribly drunk and so what you say is somewhat slurred, it will still understand you, so you can send messages, tell your TV to do things, or stuff like that just with your voice. Silent commands? Mouth reading technology so that people don't have to hear you talking to machines all the time, or speaking everything that you want written down in a 'text' or something like that.

Yeah, shit's gonna be crazy in 50 years, just look at how things have changed since 1966... I'm pretty sure that back then, a computer is something that needed an entire ROOM to fit in. Something that stored, say, 50mb of information probably weighed more than a child, or if I'm REALLY off, possibly more than a grown man. Cell phones were only around on Star Trek (if that show was around in 1966), and if car phones were around then I imagine they were expensive and possibly also low quality/connection. As for firearms, many nations still used single-stack pistols with a capacity of 7-8 rounds plus one in the chamber with the highest capacity pistol available, to my knowledge, with the magazine going into the grip of the frame, is the Hi Power with 13+1, or for Canada, 14+1 with our John Inglis mags. America had the M1911A1 (7+1 flush at the time), Germany the P1 (basically the P38 with a new name, later models getting an aluminium frame to make it lighter, 8+1), Russia the Makarov PM (8+1), and so on and so forth. 

As for rifles, America just got their XM16 design working with the M16A1 I think, the XM16 was a jammy POS and lead to the poor reputation that likes to lurk nearby in the shadows even today. Most other NATO or future NATO nations would use the FN FAL or G3, both of which use full sized rifle rounds and 20 round mags, best kept in semi auto but sometimes have full auto available as well which in my opinion is kind of stupid. The Russians and many other Combloc nations are using AK variants by now. To my knowledge, India has only just started replacing their Mk.III* Lee Enfields, albeit they're new production or at least rechambered and fire the modern 7.62 Nato cartridge instead of .303. Still, they're going with something other than a bolt action now. I think the Indian Army was one of the last major nations on the world to replace their standard issue bolt actions; Lee Enfields are JUST that good.

Sexism and racist was still pretty prominent in American society though I think other developed nations would have been faring a LITTLE bit better than them in that respect. The whole 'equal pay among the genders' thing was probably still being worked on. I don't know for sure but it's POSSIBLE that rape was a more 'hush hush' thing that it was best to just not bring up and talk about. I think even the work of 'psychology' was in its infancy back then, or at least wasn't as well documented a field, if I'm not mistaken, but I very well might be considering I'm treading into unfamiliar territory that I'm not too well studied on. Quite sure that lobotomies were still a thing in the mid 1960s. Basically, anything that third wave feminists/femi-Nazis THINK is a big deal today, was probably something that was a big deal 50 years ago that the second wave feminists have already fixed. They're driving in a fully functioning and luxurious modern vehicle and complaining that it's too loud, it has too much exhaust, the engine isn't as powerful as they'd like, there's not enough options, and the safety features are lacking. ALL THESE THINGS HAVE IMPROVED IN THE LAST 50 YEARS! Vehicles are quieter, better on the environment, more powerful, has options galore, and they're more safe than they've probably EVER been, even though vehicular accidents are still a hugely major issue in loss of human life, FAR worse than firearms.

Why I'm typing this rant up for a Filthy Frank video? I have no fucking clue, nobody will probably ever read all this, but hey, it was fun to think about as I went about it... so cringey when someone says "tl;dr". It's like standing up on a little soap box with a megaphone and yelling "THIS COMMENT IS TOO LONG FOR ME TO BOTHER READING! THE SIGHT OF AN OPEN BOOK SHOWING TWO FULL PAGES OF TEXT TERRIFIES ME! THIS IS SOMETHING I BELIEVE EVERYONE SHOULD KNOW, BECAUSE THIS PERSON TYPED A LOT OF WORDS, AND I THINK IT IS SILLY!"
